RATING: 7
I'm getting burnt on this one... any game system where you can do everything right and still have a character killed off in one round of the Overlord is just not that much fun. Heroes can roll multiple 'X' results, and the bad guys come in and do 20+ damage. Ugh. At least in Heroquest, if you were doing poorly, you had the ability to run away and escape with ease. In the second mission (ONLY THE SECOND) there's a medium boss that a hero has to do more than 6 damage in order to even hit him once. THEN he turns around and does a good 7 damage to EACH hero per swing! That's fair? I'm just tired of starting over and over and over and over...
Great combat system, great design, great bits... great everything! But seriously! I want to have fun when I play games, not be eternally frustrated. I blame the quest book, not the game system itself.

This is my original review, which despite my grumblings, still stands:
This is still the best dungeon crawl, overlord vs. player, scenario driven game I've ever played. Any of you that have read my reviews know that I'm easily swayed by imaginative elements in a game--if it makes me feel like I'm transported and in that environment, I'm  happy. So I guess that is why I was so highly impressed... this game OOZES theme. But even more than that. The combat system is incredible. It uses an alternate die format mixed with a battle-stance concept almost like a Magic Realm junior. And the artwork is, like it's brother Runebound, equally incredible. This game replaces the need for any other dungeon crawl and I'm looking forward to any expansion and other online adventures to come.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
The game moves much faster as all the players learn the flow of the game and all of the little counters, chits, and markers involved, but a full game will probably still last a few hours.  There's a good amount of fiddliness involved, but the theme is pretty rich, and the active human opponent for the heroes can keep the game pretty challenging and engaging.  While some have complained about slowdown as creatures build up, it seems that good Overlord play will eventually reduce the dependence on small monsters as the game proceeds.  I'd definitely like to try out further scenarios to see how game balance plays out.

My rating probably reflects the enjoyment of my friends, who are bigger dungeon-crawl fans than I am.  The game certainly requires a hefty investment of time, but that doesn't yet seem to discourage repeated play over a short period of time.  There is a little lack of variety for the Overlord player, but the expansions help clear that up.

RATING: 8
A dungeon crawl game using modular boards and scenarios, the game system will be an updated version of Fantasy Flight's Doom boardgame. One player acts as the dungeon master while the others take on the roles of adventurers cooperatively exploring a fantasy dungeon. The game is set in FFG's "Runebound" universe and was designed by Kevin Wilson. 16 plastic miniature heroes.

RATING: 7.4
This can be a very long and involved game the first few times playing it.  The mechanics and logistics can be a bit overwhelming as it is really an RPG made into a board game. RATING: 7.5
I enjoy Descent. 

It's a tactical Dungeon Crawl that is now starting to border on the realm of a light RPG.

The game has issues, but they don't detract from the fun. Perhaps the weakest part of the game is scenarios - some are better than others and the difficulty can vary but they're still fun especially if you are in to the theme. 

The components used to make this game are really nice, and the price of the game is well worth the quality inside. 

The rules could be organized better, and I do wish that their was a reference sheet for players detailing special abilities that some monsters have.

RATING: 8
My friends and I played through the entire campaign in short order. Not because the campaign is particularly short, but rather because once we got started, we were pretty much hooked.

While some may berate this game for being a "dumbed down" and more restrictive version of tabletop RPGing, I'd rather point out that this makes it so much more accessible, and at the same time almost as much fun.

Starting out with Descent was a major factor in getting my wife interested in D&D, so consider this a "gateway game" on the way to heavier stuff. That being said, even though my gaming group now mainly focuses on D&D, we still routinely sit down to play a Descent scenario, because it simply offers us a different experience which we enjoy.

RATING: 9.21
Comments entered on 23 Dec 2009:

Descent: Journeys in the Dark was released by Fantasy Flight Games in 2005. At the time I was a sales associate at FFG. Descent was one of the first new releases that I coordinated sales to distributors. This was an exciting time because Descent was the second "big box" game released by FFG, and there was huge buzz for its release following its introduction at GenCon.

My rating includes a number times that I demo'd this game for FFG. I have managed to play it many times with friends and with my boys. Despite all the different times I've set it up, I have as of yet to play anything except the first two scenarios and a smattering of the encounters from Road to Legend. Even with this "limited" playing, I find the game to be a fantastic example of a tactical miniatures game.

RATING: 8
A dungeon crawl game. This is the classic GM vs Players.
The game itself is very balanced and fun, and the level advancing system is just great.
Each player gets to play a unique character of choice (and there are many of them, each with its own statistics), and the GM has a very wide array of monsters at his disposal.
The only flaw in the advancement system is that magic items at higher levels are basically the same as in lower levels, but you get to roll more dice. Not very good.
Very smooth.

RATING: 2
[Played 48 times]
The core rules (mostly taken from "Doom") are decent, but would have needed a better development and much more playtesting (e.g. costs of the cards, Golden Items, etc.).
The scenarios are not very engaging (unbalanced and lacking any sort of flavour).

Being used to the GW titles (HQ, AHQ and especially WHQ), it lacks more variety of enemies, a "campaign mode" and a "random dungeon generator" (you'll need to design your scenarios, investing time and hoping to make them well).
I also miss a "magic system" worthy of this name (magic is just a different kind of ranged attack; it's as if the only known spell is "Magic Missile"... and ANY character may cast it! Despite the name, they're fireweapons, not magic).
There is a lot of randomness, but also tactical choices.

It has a more "German" approach to the dungeon crawling genre than the GW titles (e.g. optimization, resource management, simple story arc, extremely abstract town, etc.).
It also lacks much of the "dungeon crawling" feeling: you're a commando trying to rush in, grab the goodies and kill the enemies before they can react and crush you; it doesn't feel like exploring, discovering, alternating battles and lulls, etc.

Long.
It'd need too much work even to house rule it into a decent game.
Disappointing.

(2008 - BGG rating downgraded from 6 to 4)
(2013 - BGG rating downgraded to 2)

RATING: 8
I played Doom 1st Edtition, then I played Descent 1st Edition, then I thought Descent 2nd edition is better, because it is more streamlined, then Star Wars: Imperial Assault came out and I was hyped like everyone else, but now after so many years, I think this version is oddly still the best. It is not well balanced, which is its major drawback, but then again, none of the other versions is really well balanced either. So since the other version do not really improve upon Descent's weak points and even leave behind many of it's strong points, Descent 1st Edition has a certain charm and really cool mechanics, none of the other versions offer. 

For instance:
- In this version melee Heroes actually have stronger melee attacks with any melee weapon, because they add a certain number of dice to their melee attacks. The same applies to magic or ranged attacks. In the 2nd Edition any Hero can use any weapon with the same efficiency.
- In this version there are magic attacks. In the 2nd edition they left that element.

RATING: N/A
Descent: Journeys in the Dark is a semi-cooperative game in which two to five players will take on the antagonistic roles of heroes and Overlord. Up to four players will choose characters with a wide assortment of skills and innate abilities to be the heroes who will explore dungeons in search of treasure and adventure. One player will take on the role of the Overlord and will control the dungeon's many traps, puzzles, and monsters.
The heroes' goal will be to cooperatively conquer the dungeon, seize its many treasures, and achieve other objectives as set by the scenario. If the heroes cooperate and achieve their goals, they will all win. The Overlord's objective is simply to use all the means at his or her disposal - from deadly traps and ferocious monsters - to kill the heroes. Each hero has a certain Conquest Point value to the party and if too many Conquest Points are lost through hero death, the party loses and the Overlord wins.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A superb dungeon crawler game filled with theme. It borrows heavily the elements from the D&D and MMORPGs (such as monster spawns and reviving at town after death). The game has a lot of goodness such as the ability to customize your character's equipments, dungeon exploration, an overlord that makes each game a unique experience for the heroes, and challenging gameplay that results in high replay values. It also sports tons of user-made game scenarios that you can download for free. You can even create your own scenarios. On the downside, you need an overlord to control the monsters, the game does not have a 'healer' (which is crucial in an RPG setting), there isn't much of a story for each scenario, and each game can run between 2 - 6 hours. Despite the shortcomings, Descent is the best dungeon crawler board game out on the market today. Highly recommended.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
A very long, engaging game, that I really enjoy when I play with the right people.  The material is top notch and the box is full.  This is the first modern board game I bought in 2007.  I started painting all the figurines and really got into this game with my friends and we played more than 20 adventures in 2 years.  Since they moved after university, the game has collected dust a little (I am still painting the expansions, so it see the light of day once in a while).  For me, it is hard to find people who would dedicate a couple of full evening to play such a long game..  It is also noted that expansions bring the rating up for me as it add so much more stuff and options to an already jam packed game, and address some balance issues.  Speaking of balance, I believe that when the game is played the way it was intended (as a strategic positioning game, not a role playing game) it is rather well balanced (with minor houserules).  I could have won half the games I played as an overlord, but most of the time, because time was running out, I had to cut some slack on the heroes...

If you want to enjoy this game with a little more casual gamers, make sure to visite the FFG website and try some fan created missions.  Some are 2h long and very creative and fun.  I rate the base game a 7.5, but consider the expansions for more options and stuff and an advanced campain, and it's worth a 9 and my favorite game of all time.  Painted miniatures (100% complete)

RATING: 1
Good.
1. D&D adventure in 3 hours (or less).
2. Beautiful components.
3. Custom scenarios. Team match is fun (played a 2V2).

Bad
1. Overlord is boring. To make the game a FUN session for everyone, you don't want to kill the heroes early in the game where you're relatively more powerful. However, once the heroes get their silver chest, the game basically goes haywire. When they get the gold chest, there is really nothing the Overlord can do. You see inevitability, but it drags on and on.
2. Pen & Paper D&D using Miniature rules is more fun, more flexible, more free-form, and allows for more creativity. I know they are different things, just cannot help but to compare~^^
3. Fiddly? There are way too many counters. Poison, stun, web, aim, health, fatigue, etc, etc. At that level of detail you wonder why aren't you playing actual D&D.

Update: Dropped 7 Â» 6.5. "Play sporadically" due to set up and game length.

Update: Sold

RATING: 7
Pros
-I really like the diversity of characters and the way they get customized. 
- Openining treasure chests is a lot more fun than it should be :)
- Cool minis
- Some interesting tactical decisions to be made; I like the semi-cooperation aspect of the game
- This is Doom, moving in the right direction
Cons
- I preferred the Doom theme
- Seems like they overcorrected Doom; Descent felt too easy and lacked any real tension. 
- Those gold treasures are just way too overpowered

Verdict: I'm looking forwward to trying other dungeons and seeing if they get any harder. I like the overall feel of the game and the corrections they made to the spawning process and DM win mechanics, but it feels like this was an overreaction to Doom's impossible scenarios. If the other dungeons are harder than the one I've tried, I'll be happy.

RATING: 8
Descent: Jourineys in the Dark is a top quality game with a plethora of components! The atmosphere of the game is very good, and the rules are of just about the right complexity to allow for many possibilities and replayability, while still allowing a good game flow. I don't like the fact that games last veeery long - I never got it shorter than six hours with various groups! Fact is, we always had at least one new player who didn't know the rules, so it might go down to five with experienced players. The final hour of play can get a bit tiresome as everybody gets low on concentration.
My conclusion is: you can have loads of fun with Descent if you expect to have a group of at least three people who are willing to play for such a long time. And if you also like to paint minis, Descent can keep you supplied for months with decent plastic pieces! :D

RATING: 3
Okay dungeon crawl game with beautiful presentation.  I'd rate it higher but for the 'length vs. depth'.  The length is killing the fun.  After all it's just a hack n slash dice fest with an unfortunate video game feel.  That being said, the combat system is fair as is the way player turns and hero orders are resolved.  Having played magic realm and being a long time rpg player I did not find the game to be very deep or difficult to manage.  Much easier to play than even Arkham Horror for example.  I expect this game would be a big hit with younger players looking for that rpg-lite experience who don't know that playing real RPG's is much better.  Good for five players.  It could be that the expansions make this more fun.  I haven't tried them yet.  Frankly, for young people I would much rather just use Heroquest or a game that is an all around better dungeon crawl (which is most of them).  I doubt I'll ever play it as I'd much rather just play AD&D 2e or another RPG.

RATING: 8
A classic dungeon crawl adventure, Descent is beautiful to look at and great to play. The gameplay offers a meaty fantasy adventure game that is thick with theme. 

It's only real downfalls are that games tend to bog down with more players as analysis paralysis takes hold- hero players can argue over who's moving where and in what order for more then 20 minutes per turn!

It's also unweildly and very fiddley with you constantly having to reveal and add the many, many game components. Can take much longer then even Arkham Horror to play a single game!

The Overlord player is also a little over-powered when it comes to the stand alone missions and can often crush the Heroes in a couple of turns if he puts his will to it! 

These things hold it from being a 9 or 10 for me, but it's still a damn good experience though.

Trouble with regular game group attendance and negative opinions about time/fiddlyness of this one are making it difficult to hit the gaming area. Prepping not one but TWO variants with hope of being able to play it again! Sad but true.

Progressive Rating: 10-9-8-9-8-7-8.

RATING: 6
Lots of cool bits, and a good dungeon crawl. For some reason, we've never had as much fun with it as we did with Doom: the Boardgame.

(revised after several plays) - As a competitive game - not as good as Doom. After a few more plays, I don't think it's ever been much fun for anyone playing it. I like dungeon crawls as much as the next geek, but there's something about this game that always leaves everyone feeling like there should be more game to it.

It does have great components, no one has really suggested otherwise, but I really wish they were to a different game.

Edit - I have Well of Darkness now, so add the two together and the game becomes an 8 rather than a 6. It's not just more of the same - more treasure cards, overlord cards, monsters, etc.

The expansion makes some simple additions to the system  that do a lot for the fun factor of playing the overlord. Customizing the OL deck is a huge improvement. The bleed and daze status flesh out the system a lot, as does the addition of tactically different monsters like kobolds and ferrox. I'm sold on their ability to improve the game with future expansions, and when the campaign expansion comes out I think I'll have bought Altar of Despair because Well was so effective at improving the base game.

RATING: 7
I already liked Doom, and I think this is a logical improvement on that engine, wrapped in a fun fantasy, dungeon crawling RPG style dressing...

Dying three quarters into a scenario however is really not fun, neither for the overlord nor for the players. Basically it's a win for the Overlord (yay!), but it also means you don't get to play the climax encounter (booh!). And because it probably will have taken a few hours to get to that point, it's usually too much for all involved to restart the scenario. Resulting in a somewhat less that satisfactory game session for all...

My biggest caveat is that the setup and tear-down time is really, really long. For us this became an issue. In fact so much so, that we abandoned Descent in favor for actual RPG sessions.

RATING: N/A
Taking the combat system of DOOM, this dungeon crawl game has the familiar dungeon master taking on the role of the evil player, and the other players attempting to complete quests, typically destroying all the monsters in a dungeon. The combat system has been updated to be more favorable towards the players. There are 20 characters to choose from, different abiity cards dealt out at the beginning of the game, and players can spend money to acquire goods.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.7
Single best dungeon-crawl game. This game gets dungeon crawls down to how they should be. Any flaws with the game are only limitations of the genre itself. The game is well crafted in all regards. I've played them and I consider this game better than:
-HeroQuest (all versions)
-DragonStrike
-Dungeons and Dragons

This game should be seen as a superior alternative to any of these games.

Like BSG, Descent, etc. This game doesn't provide a natural incentive to move swiftly and yet, I've discovered that it's MUCH MUCH more fun when it's played quickly since it is an action--real time game simulation after all. I strongly recommend a system using timers where every player has a 1-3 minute timer which doesn't limit their entire turn but how long to take major decisions (they can still execute decisions after timer) this really speeds things up and makes things feel fun, exciting, and tense rather than just stressful, daunting, or overly drawn out. You can impose different reward/punishment incentives with health and ammo in subtle ways from the beginning so that there's incentive to move quickly but your not horribly punished if you occasionally go over.

This game, Battlestar Galactica, and Descent would all get .5 to 1 score higher with me if you use clever streamlined mechanics so that a timer for each turn is actually part of the game and at least one person knows the rules so well that he doesn't have to check rulebook ever and other people know the rules at least fairly well on top of that.

RATING: 9
I really liked this game.  A great Fantasy-Adventure game with mini's that are none other than first rate.  The rule booklet is written in typical Fantasy Flight Games style, which means that it is poorly written, but it still is a fun game.  4 adventurers seems to have things easier than 3 adventurers, which I believe to be the magic number (4) when playing this game.  Highly recommended.  It is a lengthly game though, so do plan several hours for it, especially your first time through.

I simply do not understand how others state that the game is too easy.  The Overlord regularly kicks the snot out of players, and now my gaming groups realize that no fewer than 5 people are required to play this game.  I usually play the GM as I know the rules the best, and no scenario (and I mean none) are easy for them.  I won the first scenario the first 3 times we played it.  People were getting a bit dismayed when the game was being lost by the party so often.  Now, it's about a 50-50 chance of a very experienced party making through a scenario.

RATING: 8.5
Descent just happens to hit everything I like in a game. Amazing atmosphere, great figures. Why not give it a 10? No pre-painted figures (I know, so needy) and if you play the game straight, without house rules or modifications, the game can be impossibly difficult and frustrating for the hero, as the overlord can virtually spawn new enemies each round, bogging the game down indefinitely.

The best part about the game is that the rules basically create a miniatures/battle system that can then be dropped into a more complex or expansive role-playing type game. It's possible to play any which way you like. For most, it's a straight competitive death match between players. For me, it's more about story and role-playing, switching to the regular battle mode when it's time to confront monsters.

RATING: 8

RATING: 6
 A good dungeon crawler, though its specificities sometimes alienate it from the genre. The definite change of the Overlord from a DM-like entity to an all-out opposing player was an excellent idea, which makes it more of a game than a watered down rpg. Its Doom the boardgame roots can be felt here. The rules are a bit of a mess, though, and lack fluidity and elegance. One major downside : there is no real feeling of exploration, no thrill of discovering what's hidden behind the door, since the entire dungeon is layed out at the beginning. Seems this got even worse with the second edition, were each "encounter" looks more like a tactical scenario.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
The co-operative element for the adventurers - talking through the tactical options, turn order and then executing - really helps make the theme come alive and that's a big plus over other dungeon crawlers where you're playing solo. On the down side, there aren't that many interesting decisions. Once you're equipped and your character's unique abilities are set, turns pretty much come down to the same decision - move twice, battle twice, move and battle, or be on guard. The game is one mass of fights (a fight being one simple dice roll, so at least they're quick), wading through all the baddies that the DM is setting up to stop you getting through your scenario fast. Meaning the DM arguably has the more interesting decisions - how and when to deploy - but the adventurers have the more interesting thematic ride, not knowing what's coming their way until it's sprung. Pros and cons. I can see why it's successful, and I'd play again to see if different scenarios provide a different experience, but it's way too long and not interesting enough to come out more than occasionally.

RATING: 9
A combination of Doom and Runebound. Thematically more close to runebound but the mechanics are clearly from Doom: The Boardgame.
I didn't really like Doom but this one was awesome experience. Not as good as some other FFG big box games but still extremely enjoyable. Well, this could be the best of the bigboxes, don't know yet...

The one thing I dislike a bit is the time limit. When the overlord deck exhausts, -3 conquest points, which is sometimes a lot! Well, this is absolutely better than in Doom. Since in Doom, if I remember correctly, it's instant defeat. -3 conquest points is a reasonable solution! Well, at the overlord's point of view, time limit is not so bad after all.

Another debatable issue is that if an attack misses (chances are 1/6) then it's completely missed and no way to reverse it unless attacking again. I began to like that. Because now you can't rely on building up your damage values and always score something. Makes the game a lot more exciting and aim/dodge useful!

A good thing is that there are quests varying from easy to hard, short to long. And anyone can create his own quest too. Some experienced players may even improvise the quest while playing, but that might be off-balanced quite sure... well, at least it is an option!

There is a lot to explore in this game. With all its expansions (so long, money...) it will really be a great experience with replayability rating 99%. At first I didn't appreciate this game too much, but after the second game, I began to understand its beauty and tactical possibilities.

FFG sure is the boardgame world's Blizzard: that company knows how to make a hit game for everyone to enjoy!

Edit: Counting the number of base game quests. Expansion quests / Road to Legend sessions counted in their own sites.

I wish I was 14 again, because that's probably the best age demographic that will have both the time and attention span to truly appreciate this monster.

27/03/2013: Downgraded rating to 8, in view of the really overpowered gold items (and no, I don't believe in house ruling or excluding them from the game totally)

10/04/2013: House ruling is probably the only thing that can save this game from the imbalance arising from including the gold treasures. What works to keep the intensity is to totally exclude them from the game -- doing that seems to make a hero win more fulfilling based on experience.

RATING: 3.8
I found a number of things unacceptable:
1.  The Undying characters should have some limit to their life (dying spiral - return with 1 then 2 then 3 damage, or just limit to two resurrections) - after the 6th resurrection of a sorcerer I was ready to go home.
2.  Invalidate the "Characters can't trade card."  All game we had crap for equipment and suddenly we might have gotten useful items if we could trade, but this card was played.  I laughed at all the reviews that talked about how silver and gold items make the characters unstoppable.  We sold practically every item we got.
3.  Corollary to 2:  When allowed to buy items, and buying an item in town the characters should draw two cards and get to choose one.
4.  I think the game takes too long versus the problem of balance.

What I love in 1.0, is the epicness of the game and the reminiscence that is stronger to RPGing. 1.0 is larger and more flexible than 2.0. The enemies are tougher and the overlord is able to spawn creatures. I am baffled why FFG decided to replace this. It seems to me an important ability he lost in 2.0, also making that game more easy to figure out. I also like the rules for armor better in 1.0. While I understand that they removed the old armor rules because they made you invincible at times in1.0, making it dice in 2.0 makes Armor very random.

The biggest problem I have with 1.0, is that 1.0 looks incredibly dated. 1.0 uses the old runebound/runewars mini's that have been completely replaced by 2.0, that are way better looking. 
====

Bought it again (+ expansions) after REALLY enjoying Descent 2.0 and DOOM the boardgame.

RATING: 5
A good Dungeon crawl game, but not a 'Pick-up-Game" by any stretch of the imagination.  This is a game that needs to be announced as the main course, and readily approved by all players.  The end game is in need of a large amount of help for the Overlord, as the best way to hurt characters is by charming them. Without these mods, the Overlord is only a watered down GM playing a severely simple RPG.  My frustration eith the game grows as each time the same flaws surface and each time...  experienced players EASILY kill everything in an area.  I SO wanted to love this game.

RATING: 6
Laying out the dungeon speeds play but here are a few ideas if you want to lay out the board as you play:
* Lay out the dungeon in advance, before the players come. Then put each room in labeled baggies. Label each baggie by Area number. You can include the miniatures and tokens in the baggies.
* Lay out part of the dungeon. Take a break after every two or so battles (they can get long!) and lay out the next two or so areas during the break.

Also:
* Buy a plano box (a plastic box with small areas) to hold the bits. I think a 15-section box works fine.
* Download "The Rescue" from the FFG site. It's a good introductory adventure. The first adventure in the Quest book is long and uses as many miniatures as it can from the set. IMO, You don't need really need to do that in your first game of Descent.

RATING: 6.7
This is a tabletop, map-driven, tactical role playing board-game with miniatures.  One person will take on the role of all the baddies, while the rest play the heroes.  The map is modular and grid based, and the dice mechanic is novel and very quick, one throw of the dice tell you if you hit, and for how much damage.  It's a great hack-and-slash roleplaying came which you can play without any roleplaying, however story does matter in this game as each scenario is backed by some kind of important backstory.

The main drawback I see was the amount of time it took to play, and the cost and size of the game (our game took something like 11 hours).  Setup time is also a drawback.

Make/order extra dice if possible (they are custom for the game).  The game doesn't include enough.

RATING: 7
I pretty much managed to avoid this game for a long while because it didn't really appeal to me.  The whole idea of a gamemaster that plays "against" the other players just doesn't seem right to me.  

I am very happy to have finally played the game because it is a very enjoyable experience.  It captures a lot of what I enjoyed about playing D&D/AD&D back in the day.  The whole crawling through a dungeon, killing monsters, and looking for treasure is a lot of fun.  I would be more than happy to play again.

That said, it really is a dicefest.  That's fine, as long as you are not expecting it to be something else.  I'm still not satisfied with the overlord (or whatever) implementation playing to make the players fail as it leads to some rather silly, "gamey" events, which to me detract from the overall experience.  Not sure what to do about that, though.  

Overall, though, I'm happy with the experience.  I wish it were a little cheaper, but I can see as something I would be happy to play when the opportunity presents itself. [02/14/2009]

RATING: 8

O jogo é gigante é dá o maior trabalhão.
Montar o cenário demorou quase meia hora. 
Completamente desequilibrado, os heróis matam quase todos os monstros com um acerto. 
Jogar como Overlord é até divertido.
Demora horas, eu dividi a partida em quatro sessões, uma para cada área do mesmo cenário e mesmo assim levei uns dois dias. 
Tudo meio bagunçado, as regras não são muitas mas são difíceis de lembrar.
A nota alta vai pelos componentes e seu pelo potencial criativo.
O sistema parece ser muito bom para ser adaptado e melhorado.
Oferece muitos recursos, parece uma oficina de aventuras. 

The game is huge and gives a lot of work.
Set the scene took me almost half an hour. 
Completely unbalanced, the heroes kill almost all monsters with one hit. 
To play as Overlord is kind of fun. 
It takes hours, I split the match in four sessions, one for each area of the same scenario and still took me a couple of days to complete.
Messy all around, not many rules but they are somehow difficult to remember.
I'm giving a high note by the components and it's creative potential. 
The system seems to be excellent to adapt and improve on your way. Offers many features, like a workshop of adventures.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
It is difficult for me to give a fair opinion of this game.  Certainly with the right people this can be fun, and the system is strikingly clean and easy to understand.  It really boils down the new style of d20 dungeon crawls into primal elements, and really does a great job of recreating an "adventure".  But as someone that actually plays RPGs this feels like just the framework to a house, a good solid frame, but you don't really want to live there.

The reason that RPG's are fun is that you can do anything creative that you want.  I walk into a room there is a big lizard and I release 5 chickens.  The lizard runs around confused trying to get the chickens now I've got the drop on it, etc.  But in Descent you stock yourself up with whatever would make you get the best rolls on the dice.  Soon you are just munchkining out rolling obscene amounts of damage.  The first thing you do is run to the chest, see if anything in it will help you beat the bad guys then whack 'em.  There are some tactics certainly, but most of the battles come down to:  

I'm going to shoot my bow. 
[Roll] 
Did it get arrowed? 
No.  
I'll try again. 
[Roll]
Yup, you did one heart worth of damage.
I'll use a fatigue.
Ok, roll again.
[Roll]
One more damage, he gets a heart.
One more fatigue.
[Roll]
Nope, didn't work this time. 
Darn, your turn.

Repeat, repeat, repeat, repeat. 

To me there is nothing more tedious than listening to a role-player retell their past gaming adventures.  After the first few minutes you realize this is going to be a long "story" that does nothing to add to your life experience.  

The biggest flaw of the game is that you don't really care if your character dies.  Something seems wrong about that to me.

Now that said, because of the downtime, the system is conducive for friends to sit around for 8 hours and just gab, while playing something light and incidental.  If I were to equate this to anything I would say that this is the geek version of sports parties where buddies all go over to watch the game and really just use it as an excuse to hang out with each other while something entertaining occupies the dead space.  There are moments of excitement, and certainly with the right group this can be fun, but if you want something stimulating or short look elsewhere.

I can't imagine wanting to play this more that once or twice.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Played 10+  times

The atmosphere is great. The bits are great, the theme is great. Character management is fun. Combat is fine.

Game progression is out of whack. The first part of the game feels just right. The heroes must work together, and there is a real sense of danger. The game tilts as the heroes gain treasures. This is a real problem. The toughest monsters are no match for the toughest treasures. End game often has the heroes waltzing into a room, using an uber-item, and watching dragons and giants disintegrate.

For the overlord to win, he must delay the heroes in order to cycle through the deck and remove conquest tokens. This results in heroes fighting wave after wave of weak spawned monsters. The monsters have no hope of killing the heroes after they obtain silver and gold armor. So, battles become incredibly repetitive and tedious for both the overlord and heroes. 

As overlord, I often find myself NOT spawning creature after hours of repetitive fighting, just to get the game over with. I still must sit through the rest of it just to get to the inevitable ending where the heroes finally reach a room full of dragons and creatures that might actually pose a threat. But alas, they really don't pose a threat because by the time the heroes get that far they have such powerful uber items that they just waltz into the final room, use their, "Rune of immediate disintegration of all creatures ever invented or imagined within three solar systems" and game over.

The 2nd edition totally eliminates all the negatives from this first edition, keeps the good stuff, and adds some pure awesomeness.

RATING: 4
An airing of grievances:

1) Takes 3-4 hours to barrel through a full scenario, not including the time it takes to set up and break down.

2) There's no sense of drama or mounting tension. Adventures always start out tough on the players, and once they grab silver/gold items it's a cakewalk from there on out. The end game seems to drag on endlessly as the mists of story and atmosphere dissipate, revealing a  clunky hack-and-slash dice-off.

3) No control over character advancement. Characters don't actually improve; they just loot more powerful swag. Goodies are drawn randomly from various Treasure Decks which often leads to situations where characters will draw completely useless items (i.e. melee fighters drawing Runes), thereby not advancing their power level and making further reaches of the dungeons even more of a grind.

4) LOS spawning system is very, very irritating. Example: Our party once spent forty-five minutes of real time clearing the baddies out of a room with a single door only to walk through that doorway, lose LOS into that room, and then watch in horror as hordes of skeletons marched out of it the following turn. This makes no sense and guts any sense of accomplishment you might get from smashing bad guys.

For a game that tries to do so much, it's disheartening to see it fall short. I've read that the expansions improve on the base game quite a bit, but until the dude in our group who owns Descents picks any of them up, I've got to stick this rating. For the time you've got to put in to make this work, I'd rather play D&D.

RATING: 7
[FFG 05 edition] {Fantasy adventure; dice-rolling, scenario, modular board, fighting, devil vs. angel} I like RPG games. Therefore, I am particularly interested in adventure game. However, it's really not easy to find decent adventure games because it's difficult to design and needs many expansions / add-ons to have good replay values. Usually, adventure games work better at computers.

Descent comes under my radar. It looks nice and gorgeous. It also interests because the role of Overlord - it seems like DM and has rival teams. Besides, it should have better replayability for its scenario construction (like Settlers), many heroes and skills. I am happy that I have bought it because it's a really decent adventure game: full of fun, thematic and supporting role-playing; though the fun of the game depends heavily on the setup of the quest, players and Overload.

The game system is effective and it really supports interaction between players and Overlord. So far, the skills are limited. I expect more and more expansions will be released.

I hope that Descent supports more players so that we can more adventure experience. I also hope that each hero can have different roles / attributes other than different abilities or stats so that a better teamwork can be fostered (some tasks need different heroes to complete). Further, I hope that heroes can be non-human so that some heroes may have special ability or weakness. Can there any invisible monsters / traps too? Umm, adding all these will make Descent become an AD&D game ...

[Expansions] Both expansions are good to have. They add new capability, fun and strategies to the basic game.

RATING: 6
Several plays in, the game works pretty well. I enjoyed it enormously and look forward to future play-throughs. The production values are incredible and the gameplay strikes a nice balance between tactics and pure hack-n-slash dice rolling. It has the sentiment of D&D's lineage but the intuitive design and streamlining of modern board-gaming. If only that intuitive elegance extended to the rulebook and balancing rather than just the components and mechanics--Descent is no better and no worse in this sense than Arkham Horror or any other Fantasy Flight endeavor. 

Balance is wonky so far. The first two-thirds of the In the Dark were a cakewalk for the heroes. The final third saw almost all of their conquest tokens dissolved, but more through my effective use of threat and a REALLY well timed Dark Charm than anything in the dungeon--the final boss monster was taken down very quickly and the heroes were one-shotting all of my other most powerful monsters.

I've been digging through the fan-made Cataclysm series with much more success, and I will eventually work up to building my own dungeons. I also have yet to try being a hero. Despite my quibbles, if every game went about like my first run of In the Dark, I would consider my money well spent. And with better vanilla dungeons and some of the fan work out there, things are only improving.

RATING: 6
Got the original game of this with no expansions on a semi-whim.  Rules were a lot to go through, and the online updates/FAQ were also a lot to know.  There's a lot of corner cases and things it took us awhile to get.  With that said, the actual game was quite fun.  Good old dungeon-crawler, with a dungeon keeper thrown in also. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
As a kid/teenager, I played MB's HeroQuest and roleplaying games.
And just when I thought "They should do a game like HeroQuest again", FFG published DOOM and Descent.
The game looks beautiful, and compared to HeroQuest offers far more tactical depth. It was also refreshing that the Overlord is a real opponent for the hero players, and not just a storyteller or the guy to bring the hero fodder into position.
There are a lot of different characters to play (especially with the expansions), with different stats and special abilities. A lot of skills bring even more versatility, as do the different special items that are to be found in the dungeon. This all adds to the replay-value of the game. Even if you were to play the same scenario again and again,it will be with a different group of heroes every time, and they all will need their very own approach and tactics.
Some people complain about the game being too long, and I can see where they are coming from - but I don't mind playing for hours when I'm enjoying myself.

RATING: 7
We had our first run last night and I was the Overlord.  It was the first mission and they ran through it pretty easy, however we all enjoyed the playing of it.  It is difficult to be Overlord when introducing as you have that conflict of wanting to make sure the enjoy the game yet at the same time trying to kick their butts.In the end I probably went a bit too easy and they finished with 13 conquest tokens left.After a few plays we use the following house rules:1) Portals are assigned a 50gp or 100gp portal cost - the starter portal is always free2) Players choose two hero cards, get choice of their own draw first.  You can choose from ANY of the drawn cards however.3) Players must take items found in chests back to town and sell at half price if they don't want them.  There is no exchange for money at full value.

RATING: 7
2/21/06 - Rating pending first play.

3/5/2006 - This is an Excellent game. The battle system is excellent. The extensive play-testing is apparent in the fluid mechanics of the game. Everything is balanced and each time you come across a new part of the game and see the balance in action realization of why it was setup in such a manner hits you with a little smirk. This has everything that makes you interested in D&D and none of the baggage that makes you say that you will NEVER play D&D! The pieces are amazing, the box is the perfect size to pack all the pieces. The only reason this doesn't get a 10 is the fact that it is a Co-op all vs. one game and it lacks some of the strategic components I would like in a PERFECT game. However, it is a SOLID 9!

RATING: 6
A very nice dungeon cralwer. The rules are complex but not too dificult and are easy enough once you get the hang of it. The components are great (of course) and I really like the fact, that the Overlord is *not* an Dungeonmaster (in the sense of RPGs) but a competitive player.
The main drawback is the missing campaign system. Another thing that bothers me a bit, is the long playing time that also is hard to calculate (Depending on the circumstances a certain adventure can vary in lenght significantly). I like long games but this one can draw out too long. I am yet undecided on the balance issue because I have only played the game four times yet. I don´t expect total balance anyway, but to me it seems, that the game is definitly in favour of the heroes (four Heroe victories out of four games).
07/21/07 update: After some more play, the game seems heavily in favour of the overlord in the later quests. Not quite sure, how this can be balanced or if the heroes play badly.
01/01/15 update: Great game - but Imperial Assault is way better! Lowered score from 9 to 7.

VS 2nd edition

RATING: 7
The rating for this is only temporarily, expected to shift upwards with advancing quests. I was playing the overlord twice. With the first quest resulting in two parts of the game. The first half of it was the heroes storming the dungeon, wiping away my monsters at single stroke or if not, using one of multiple talents/weapons (maybe there are too many) to do with the monster before a counteratttack. That way they moved through the dungeon, reducing my actions almost to only setting up the rooms and nothing else in a 4-hour time span. Oh yeah, I could play a card from time to time and sometimes even got to finish of their weakest player. Second "half" (maybe 5 minutes) of the game was the heroes opening the Big Boss' room. I played some cards, the giant swept around, kiling two heroes at once, taking away all of the heroes tokens. That was the game. The second quest however was much better balanced, very tense and with every side having its chances for victory, moving back and forth. What more, it turned out to be, that levelling up is much harder than in other fantasy games (say Talisman, Runebound, World of warcraft) That's not bad. Yet, if you do want to actually see your hero progress from wimp to pimp, you might be better off with one of the other games.

RATING: 9.5
My friend played Hero Quest with his older brother as a kid. A few years ago, he got a copy of it off of ebay for $50. I played it for the first time that Christmas. I loved it! Fighting monsters, collecting treasure, and slaying bosses. Epic.......... until I realized that there was a game that was Hero Quest on steroids. That game is Descent. This game is the dungeon crawl to end all dungeon crawls. The game is so immersive. When it's set up, people are drawn to it. Every single person that has played it so far has loved the game. If you have a friend who has even the slightest interest in anything geeky like LOTR or even video games, try this game with them. I read the forums and all the comments on how the game's rules are awful. I studied up on the rules and have yet to have a rules debate. Don't be afraid of the price either, if you have any interest in this game at all, get it. Awesome minis, Beautiful board, great components. This is, by far, my favorite game to date.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Descent only loses points due to its length; this one takes a long time.  A group of veteran players can hammer through a scenario, but any kind of casual game can definitely last several (ie, more than 4) hours.

The game has great components, characters, monsters, and the rules work well.  The different color dice are great for combat, and present a more understandable mechanic to new players.

The game can be a little frustrating for the DM, as players tend to mow-down your minions with ease, especially once they have a few magic items available.

Overall, a fun game which players really seem to enjoy.

**Please note that the Road to Legend expansion jacks this game up to a 10 for me.***

RATING: 9
Descent: Journeys in the Dark is a semi-cooperative game in which two to five players will take on the antagonistic roles of heroes and Overlord. Up to four players will choose characters with a wide assortment of skills and innate abilities to be the heroes who will explore dungeons in search of treasure and adventure. One player will take on the role of the Overlord and will control the dungeon's many traps, puzzles, and monsters.

It is not uncommon for monsters to get cut down before they even get a real attack, but despite this, I was still able to keep the players on the edge through most of the first scenario.  About the only real knock on this game is the length.  It is probably the right length for this sort of game, but it still will make it hard to get out again.  We have to organize multiple play sessions in a row to make it work.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The rule book is a pain to look through.  The rules themselves are ok once you know where to find things (I'm still learning).  Your best bet is to grab the consolidated rules here on BGG and reference that.

One thing I haven't liked are the condition of the bits.  The interlocking corridors don't seem to always want to interlock very well.  You have to press and adjust things to get them to stay together.  If this was a puzzle, I would have taken it back to the store if that says anything.  My set contained a Naga that was decapitated, a spider that was broken off of his base, and a skeletal archer missing part of his bow.  The packing for these figures could stand some improvement.  Another, personal pet peeve, is that there are a TON of tokens and counters to keep track of.  Keeping a handle on all of these for a first timer is a bit much.  Finally, one strangeness with the cards is that the blue die appears to be purple.  At first I thought we were missing a die, but it's just shoddy coloring on the printer's part.  This is very annoying.

As far as the game goes, the mechanics are simple and my sons and I enjoy playing it.  I've played this with an 8-year old and an 11-year old.  The 11-year old is really shining with tactical concepts which is fun.  They both are *REALLY* good at remember board set up from the previous plays -- pointing out where all the treasures and potions should go while I'm still referencing the map in the quest book.  The 8-year old tends to ignore his skill cards and we've not been using the order markers -- that's just too much for either of them.  Even so, they do pretty well.

So that makes up for the problems with the bits, I guess.  I bought it on-line for $50.  Had I got it from my LGS (notice the lack of the 'F') at the $80 MSRP, I would have felt ripped off.

RATING: N/A
[Played 48 times]
The core rules (mostly taken from "Doom") are decent, but would have needed a better development and much more playtesting (e.g. costs of the cards, Golden Items, etc.).
The scenarios are not very engaging (unbalanced and lacking any sort of flavour).

Being used to the GW titles (HQ, AHQ and especially WHQ), it lacks more variety of enemies, a "campaign mode" and a "random dungeon generator" (you'll need to design your scenarios, investing time and hoping to make them well).
I also miss a "magic system" worthy of this name (magic is just a different kind of ranged attack; it's as if the only known spell is "Magic Missile"... and ANY character may cast it! Despite the name, they're fireweapons, not magic).
There is a lot of randomness, but also tactical choices.

It has a more "German" approach to the dungeon crawling genre than the GW titles (e.g. optimization, resource management, simple story arc, extremely abstract town, etc.).
It also lacks much of the "dungeon crawling" feeling: you're a commando trying to rush in, grab the goodies and kill the enemies before they can react and crush you; it doesn't feel like exploring, discovering, alternating battles and lulls, etc.

Long.
It'd need too much work even to house rule it into a decent game.
Disappointing.

(2008 - BGG rating downgraded from 6 to 4)
(2013 - BGG rating downgraded to 2)

RATING: N/A
Across the land, courageous heroes delve into shadowed dungeons, journey to lost cities, and explore forgotten ruins. In the darkest corners of the world, these heroes confront deadly and terrifying monster, including Skeletons, Hell Hounds, Giants, Demons, and Dragons. For those few who survive, the rewards are many. Victorious heroes return from the treacherous dungeons with ancient magics, bags of gold, and powerful weapons and artifacts.
\13\\13\
In Descent: Journeys in the Dark, you play on of these daring adventurers. Armed with mighty weapons and powerful abilities, you venture into the dungeon to battle monsters, escape deadly traps, discover lost treasures, and ultimately, confront and defeat the evil masters that dwell in the hidden place. Can you survive the dark?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This game is something the fantasy genre has needed for a long time. A dungeon delve that focuses on combat, with a Dungeon Master who doesn't have to be bored "challenging" players but not really hurting them. In Descent, the DM is not your friend...He wants to kill your character and laugh while doing it.

The game is a lot of fun and does a nice job of managing the two sides of the conflict. My only real complaint about it is that the monsters the Overlord (DM) gets to spawn are incredibly easy to kill. There isn't nearly as much tactical maneuvering as I expected, because most of the critters go down in one shot. The best use of your monsters is usually to charge straight ahead and try to overwhelm the heroes with sheer numbers.

Occasionally a monster does spawn with an opportunity to do something creative, but those moments are few and far between. I know the designers wanted to keep things simple and clean, but I think in this case it ended with a missed opportunity. The heroes also power up exceptionally fast, which adds to the problem. By the middle of the game the Overlord is usually reduced to playing trap cards on the team's weakest member to try and score kills. It's still fun, just not nearly as satisfying as it could be.

It's a cool idea for a game and it comes with buckets of plastic miniatures. You could do a whole lot worse than Descent to get your fantasy gaming fix.

RATING: 5
HISTORY: I first came across this game in 2006 when I played it at a friend's place. Back then it struck me as hopelessly complex. In the years since I took to D&D 3rd and 4th edition (after a long RPG hiatus from my childhood), and got used to more complex games. When revisiting Descent in 2009, the game struck me as fairly easy to digest and grok, if also largely pedestrian. This is D&D's younger brother in most regards, for better or ill. 

Now that it's 2012, with a second edition on the horizon, I grabbed two cheap copies of the first edition, one for myself, one for my nephews. It's really my experiences of the game with them that account for how I view and rate the game today. See recorded plays, especially no. 1.

RATING: In a nutshell, great components, especially the dice and the adorable minis. The rules the game comes with are at best functional and miss all that matters in D&D (perception and parley rolls, among others). With due adjustments it's fairly easy to create memorable gaming experiences with this. But out of the box, I rate this a 5/10, and frankly that's generous.

RATING: 6
A generally (though not completely) improved version of Doom, although the game loses points for being so darn long.  Due to time constraints, I can't imagine playing Descent more than 10 times in my life.

Update:

I hit the 10-play mark!  My kids like the game, and it hits the table occasionally at cons and game nights.  I may actually hit 20 plays before death.  So sue me.

For those hoping to improve balance issues, we always use the following variants: (1) threat costs on spawn cards are [i]per figure[/i], with the overlord having the option to spawn fewer than the maximum # of figures - although any master figures are always spawned last, and (2) killing the same hero twice in a row results in the overlord receiving half the number of conquest tokens, rounded down.

RATING: N/A
Описание: Покорение подземелья одного игрока командой приключенцев других игроков
Суть: разведка подземелья, убийство толп монстров, призыв толп монстров, сбор экипировки, броски кучи кобиков.
Сложность: средняя, объясняется за 30 минут.
Игроков: 2-5, один из них играет против всех остальных. Лучше 4-5.
Тип: тактика 50%, удача 30%, стратегия 20%
Длительность: 1-4 часа
Оформление: очень хорошее.

Великолепная игра. Поначалу. Но потом она мне очень сильно надоела и разонравилась. Не все от нее так быстро устают, и я часто даю игру поиграть кому-нибудь еще, чтобы не просили меня в нее играть. Интересна сама идея игры: устроить противостояние мастера подземелья и героев по строгим правилам (а не как в D&D - на волю DMа). Чем больше подземелье, тем игра затянутей, в гигантские играть совершенно невозможно.

RATING: 7
If you have the time and the money to invest, I am pretty sure Descent is the dungeon crawler game to get.  The painted miniatures, the 3D map boards and all the other accessories really do add to the experience.  Unfortunately, it also means extra time for setup and tear down as you recreate each floors.  The whole process isn't as bad if you have a capable DM running the show with people that can make decisions without too much AP, but even then there is plenty of downtime, and I cannot imagine playing this with newcomers that aren't able to grasp the concepts very quickly.

I enjoy the different type of dice and how they represent range, damage and whether special abilities can trigger.  The line of sight rule is a bit perplexing to me, but I usually leave it to the other people to determine.  Descent is a great game to pull out once in a while when you crave a bit of mayhem and battles.

RATING: 10
This is one of my absolute favorite games ever!  It is truly complex and offers some pretty intense game sessions.  Although many people consider this to be a rip off of other games, I think every game is guilty of that in some way or another in terms of mechanics.  I, on the other hand, disagree with the statement.

The production value of this is amazing!  Having an insane amount of miniatures included really takes this over the top!  I cannot praise this game enough!

The game play is excellent as either a hero or the overlord.  Both sides of the spectrum are fanastic and very well balanced, in my opinion.  If you do, however, encounter some issues of balance, the expansions do a very good job ironing it out.

The components are perfect in every sense of the word. As mentioned, the miniatures included are very detailed and high quality.  The artwork which adorns everything included in the box is stunning and highly thematic.  I am very pleased.

This has to be my favorite Fantasy Flight game to date!

RATING: 3
This game is a huge time vacum that just leaves me drained.  It's funny, because I don't mind long, epic games, but in Descent, it takes hours and hours to make the tiniest bit of progress.  It's not epic at all, it's just a inefficient game system that demands a lot and returns little.  There are millions of games out there that accomplish way more with much less.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A great fantasy tactical game. You need a cooperative group since the rules are somewhat ambiguous. If you can chase away the rules lawyers, it becomes a lot more fun.

The components can double as dungeon tiles for D&D.

I recently bought my own copy. Set-up can take a bit, so it's best to be prepared in advance. Like with Twilight Imperium, this is a game that it's best to schedule an evening around.

RATING: 7.5
A very good fantasy version of Doom, which I initially felt was better than its predecessor - and its true, they have polished and tightened a lot of the rules.  However, there are a few balance issues which  badly need to be fixed.  Halfway through a dungeon, after a coupla bronze or silver chests, the heroes are SO hard nothing is even vaguely a challenge.  However, the minis are ace, it looks brilliant, and is fun to play.  Games are a touch on the long side sadly, takes around 3 hours per dungeon.
